Russell Senior, Secretary
russell at personaltelco.net


From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Jan 20 14:19:24 2009
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Tue, 20 Jan 2009 14:19:24 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] IOGEAR GCS1764 DVI USB KVM
Message-ID: <20090120221924.GA26811@gate.kl-ic.com>

"IOGEAR GCS1764 DVI USB KVM" - with everything officially all
caps, it sounds like I am shouting, doesn't it?

No questions here, just some experiences.

As part of my office cleanup, I put DVI-output video cards into
all my tower machines, and connected to them through an IOGEAR 
four port digital KVM, feeding a Viewsonic flat screen.  The 
old Gateway VX900 (rebranded Hitachi CM1711, IIRC ) CRT
monotor is now in storage.  More deskspace, less heat.

Like all DVI KVMs, startup order is important - first the 
monitor, then the KVM, then the computers.  The computers must
be selected during boot for the KVM to learn about them.  

The 4 port GCS1764 was on openbox sale at Frys for $162 - they
are on sale at Newegg for $175 with free shipping.  The unit
comes with 4 cable sets, with only the digital video routed.
If you want to route analog video, the box may support it, 
but you will need your own cables (if you are routing analog
video, buy a cheaper analog switch!).  The cables also carry
one USB path, and stereo audio in and out.   There is also
a serial cable for downloading firmware upgrades to the box,
but no downloadable firmware on the IOGEAR site.

The GCS1764 is a bit quirky - apparently it won't talk properly
to NVidia chipsets integrated on motherboards (a USB problem). 
The device has two ports for USB mouse and keyboard on the front.
The front USB ports don't work right for me -  the keyboard will
occasionally behave like it has a stuck key, and repeat.  However,
there are two USB ports on the back, intended for sharing other
peripherals, that work fine for the keyboard.  The KVM (actually
called a "KVMP", and thus a little hard to find on the Newegg
site) controls are a little quirky - four buttons in front.  You
must push and hold the switch for about 5 seconds (!) to make it
switch both the video and the back USB ports. 

The GCS1764 manual explains setting the device up with hotkeys;
however, the keyboard must be connected to the front USB port
for this to work.  I would rather just push the front buttons.

So the IOGEAR GCS1764 KVMP is a little quirky, but it is a lot
better than a bunch of monitors.  If you can put the unit on
your desktop, and the computers are close enough for the 6
foot cables to reach, and the conditions above are met, it will
save you some power and desk space.

BTW, for my wife's new office computer, I bought an IOGEAR two
port USB DVI KVM, assuming I would need to switch between a net
connected Linux EEE and an isolated WinXP EEE.  Now that I have
Dragon Naturally Speaking working under VMWare, I can achieve 
the same isolation with proper passwording and encryption on
one machine.  That KVM worked fine, too.

Keith

That helped. It showed that the desktop was still expecting to connect
to 192.168.0.102, when the laptop was -.101. I looked in the exports
file on the desktop and it showed -.101. So then I did
"/etc/init.d/networking restart" on the desktop. But afterwards the
showmount command on the laptop still showed the desktop insisting that
it would connect only to -.102.

Finally, I rebooted the desktop again (about three times now). And then
the showmount command reflected the correct exports. And then I was
finally also able to mount the partitions on the laptop. Whew!

Curious that restarting the network did not update the exports. Oh
well. I am now much better off because each machine has a fixed address
so the command should never fail again. Thanks to all for the advices.

Tim is correct you need to restart the NFS daemon on the machine that is
exporting to clients in order for the changes in /etc/exports to take
effect, restarting networking will only do something meaningful if you
changed the IP address for the NIC/Wireless card etc.

/usr/sbin/exportfs -r -v

Failing is expected.  What is more surprising is an update billed as a
recommended action to *prevent* premature failure actually causing
immediate failure of what was previously an apparently functioning
drive.  And then having that followed up by pretty much total silence
about the problem, not providing a way to immediately revert whatever
/sbin/fsckage their broken update did, etc.  That is a monumental,
viability-threatening event in the life of a company.

From mike at mommabears.com  Tue Jan 20 22:01:31 2009
From: mike at mommabears.com (MJang)
Date: Tue, 20 Jan 2009 22:01:31 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] The Ubuntu Hard Drive Killing Bug Fixed (I hope)
Message-ID: <1232517691.4983.10.camel@UbuntuHH>

Folks, 

Somewhat related to the Seagate thing is the Ubuntu hard drive bug -
fixes are being released for various Ubuntu releases, through updated
acpi-support packages. 

When I first saw the bug, I checked the number of cycles on my hard
drive with the following command:

$ sudo smartctl -a /dev/sda | grep 193

which reveals the "Load_Cycle_Count". If I remember right, the typical
load cycle count lifetime is about 600,000 cycles. When I checked it on
a fairly new hard drive (less than 2mo) on my Dell e1405, it was at
180,000 cycles. I thought, oh S$(*! and tinkered until I found this fix
which I put in my /etc/rc.local

hdparm -B 200 /dev/sda

But now, everything should be OK with the latest update.

For more info, see
https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/acpi-support/+bug/59695 

Thanks,
Mike

$  sudo apt-cache search smartctl
smartmontools - control and monitor storage systems using S.M.A.R.T.

$ apt-cache search smartctl

which should lead to the following message:
smartmontools - control and monitor storage systems using S.M.A.R.T.

Then 

$ sudo apt-get install smartmontools

From creswick at gmail.com  Wed Jan 21 09:48:04 2009
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Wed, 21 Jan 2009 09:48:04 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Alternatives to gnome-power-manager
Message-ID: <c834ec80901210948q395cf992g7d6b3ad469735232@mail.gmail.com>

I run a number of ubuntu/debian laptops that use Enlightenment DR17 as
the window manager / desktop environment, and since ubuntu ~7 or so
(and about the same time for debian) I've only been able to get the
power-management features to work under these configurations by
running gnome-power-manager in the background.  This has the following
advantages:

* suspend/resume "just works"
* I can configure the power management settings fairly easily (as long
as the settings I want to configure have been deemed "important" to
the Gnome Dieties.)
* Things like screen dimming when unplugging the AC, etc. work
* the screen brightness and volume controls make use of some On-screen
display that looks fairly clean.
* etc..

However, gnome-power-manager crashes frequently.  It often dies when I
unplug the power, leaving the screen brightness OSD on-screen untill I
kill the process, or at times all or some of the above features will
simply stop working.  <rant> In short, I'm sick of babysitting it, and
I'd much rather support a project that has a better design.  IMHO,
power-management has no place in a Desktop Manager, and had this been
designed "properly" then the Gnome power manager would be nothing but
a snazzy UI for some background WM-agnostic daemon that did the actual
work. (Maybe there are some good reasons for this, but I have been
unable to discern any other than ease of implementation.)</rant>

Does anyone know of other applications / daemons / etc. I could try in
order to get similar functionality?

Thanks!
Rogan

From raanders at cyber-office.net  Wed Jan 21 13:56:58 2009
From: raanders at cyber-office.net (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Wed, 21 Jan 2009 13:56:58 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Stopping ssh brute force attacks
Message-ID: <49779A2A.9080401@cyber-office.net>

There have been several threads about handling the ssh login floods
especially the noise that gets into /var/messages.

Well I found and have tested an Iptables solution.  Works quite nice.

I run CentOS 5.x systems so I can't say how to get this into other
iptables but here it goes.

This is an excerpt from a working /etc/sysconfig/iptables file. 
Redhatian users should recognize the first four lines.   This is where I
put it on my systems.  I still have to figure out how to make it hold
for longer than the 60 seconds.
    I also changed syslog to use /var/log/iptables for the
SSH-Brute_force messages.  You could just take the LOG statement out and
then only see actual attempts.

I've added blank lines to make the MUA induced wrap standout.  This is
based on the information I found at
	http://www.la-samhna.de/library/brutessh.html
Which is based on
	http://blog.andrew.net.au/2005/02/16#ipt_recent_and_ssh_attacks


### Begin
-A INPUT -j RH-Firewall-1-INPUT

-A FORWARD -j RH-Firewall-1-INPUT

-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -i lo -j ACCEPT

-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -p icmp --icmp-type any -j ACCEPT

#+# 20090120raa - Handle brute force assaults.
# Add a chain to hold ips that you don't want to block no matter what

-N SSH_WHITELIST

# add one (faked for this posting)

-A SSH_WHITELIST -s 192.168.0.42 -m recent --remove --name SSH -j ACCEPT

-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -p tcp --dport 22 -m state --state NEW -m recent
--set --name SSH

-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -p tcp --dport 22 -m state --state NEW -j
SSH_WHITELIST

-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -p tcp --dport 22 -m state --state NEW -m recent
--update --seconds 60 --hitcount 4 --rttl --name SSH -j LOG --log-prefix
"SSH_brute_force"

-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -p tcp --dport 22 -m state --state NEW -m recent
--update --seconds 60 --hitcount 4 --rttl --name SSH -j DROP
###


Enjoy,
Rod


From keithl at kl-ic.com  Wed Jan 21 23:40:49 2009
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Wed, 21 Jan 2009 23:40:49 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Jax dining room going away
Message-ID: <20090122074049.GB4815@gate.kl-ic.com>

Jax is effectively going away in February.

Tonight after Advanced Topics, Alan and I talked with Barb Davis,
co-owner of Jax.  Her landlord won't let her have the large
dining room area at a price she can afford, so it disappears at
the end of January.  We have been using the room for advanced 
topics, and general meeting afters.  POSSE and Personal Telco
also use it for their monthly meetings.  Jax will have a small
room available, seating 10 people, behind the kitchen.  Not 
big enough, and not available until March or April or so.

So, the hunt is on for another venue.  We need free, and a place
we can set up a projector and screen.  The ideal site (which we
are probably not going to find) would have these characteristics:

   1)  Free (unless you volunteer pay for it yourself)
   2)  Seating between 10 and 40
   3)  Reasonably quiet
   4)  Affordable food and beer until 11pm or so
   5)  Not too far from downtown
   6)  Parking
   7)  MAX within walking distance
   8)  Wifi (though we might help them set this up)
   9)  Screen  ("")
  10)  Projector ("")

That is my ordering, YMMV.  If there is a screen and projector,
I get to use MAX myself.  Some places (like McMenamins) are
free if we order enough food, but sometimes advanced topics
doesn't draw a big crowd, while other times we fill the room. 
On the small crowd nights, we don't want to hit the organizers
and speakers with a bill for the difference.

I imagine we will continue to schedule the general meeting on
the first thursday, but we can probably move the Advanced 
Topics meeting to monday or tuesday if necessary.  We can use
two different venues, of course, but we lose some leverage. 
Moving will cost us some attendees, while enabling others, but
may be necessary if that is the only time a venue is available.

I like ethnic restaurants, but many of you do not.  I live in
Beaverton, but a move away from downtown would mean many of
you would no longer appear.  Overall, I will gladly forgo
many of my preferences if it means more of you show up.

Ideas combined with action are 50x better than ideas phrased
as "we should" or "why don't you ...".  If you think of a
place, please contact the proprietor and see what the cost
arrangements are, what nights are free, etc.  Then share what
you learn with the list.  The first solid idea, soonest, wins!

And send a big thank you to Barb and the people at Jax.  This
is tough for them, too, and they have taken great care of us
for a long time.  If any of you are rich, buy the building
from her landlord, and lower her rent so we can stay...

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

Recessions stink!!  I have some good friends who closed their down town
restaurant about a year ago because of a combination of increased rents,
disruptive street construction, and simply not getting enough customers.

More to the point, we need to find a new location.
I think we should keep as many of our meetings at their normal times
if at all possible.  We have the room at PSU scheduled and reserved
for us on the first Thursday of the month for the foreseeable future.
I'm reluctant to change this - unless we have to.

Would it make any sense to go back to the Lucky Lab?
Of course, the Lucky Lab has noise problems - and they weren't willing
to give us the meeting room for free.  However given this recession,
they maybe willing to reconsider.  Should I talk to them?

David Mandel

How inconvenient would the Pepper Mill near Kinnaman and Farmington in
Aloha be to people? They have a large back room, good food at reasonable
prices and some alcohol, though they are not a brewpub. It is quiet --
too quiet, actually. I don't know about a projector or screen. There is
lots of free parking. I don't think they have wifi. I don't know if they
charge extra for the room -- I can ask them if there is some consensus
on the Tri-Met issue noted below.

I think the big gotcha will be Tri-Met. There is a bus that goes by, but
I am uncertain of the night schedule and it is a "milk run" between the
Beaverton and Willow Creek transit centers.

http://trimet.org/schedules/r052.htm


In short -- great place, convenient for Beaverton/Aloha/Hillsboro folks
with vehicles but not necessarily for anyone else. So if you're a
Tri-Met person, hit up the trip planner, see if it would work for you
and let me know. The address is

17455 SW Farmington Rd # 26B
Aloha, OR 97007
(503) 642-5193

I may check out the "upscale" restaurants at Beaverton Central MAX
station tonight, since I'm going to be at OTBC for a meeting. I don't
have much hope for that because they look expensive, but I might be wrong.

http://calagator.org/events/1250456514

-- 
M. Edward (Ed) Borasky

Note to Drivers #2:  Do not turn left on 23rd.  Instead, make a wide
U-turn (as if you were going to go back up to the Fremont Bridge),
then immediately take the Thurman St. exit.  Turn right at the first
stop sign (19th St.).  Proceed 3 blocks south and turn right onto
Quimby for the front entrance.  Or, from the Thurman/19th stop sign, 
proceed only 2 blocks south and turn right onto Raleigh, which gives
access to the big parking lot in the back of the Lab.

As nice as the NW Lab is, I suspect the meeting room at the original
Hawthorne location is a better fit.  IIRC, the NW Lab won't let you
have their room for free.

- Don
... currently employed at iMove, Inc. at 1732 NW Quimby,
     conveniently located only 2 blocks east of the NW Lab

Kurt Sussman wrote:
> Roderick A. Anderson (raanders at cyber-office.net) typed this ...
>> There have been several threads about handling the ssh login floods
>> especially the noise that gets into /var/messages.
>>
>> This is an excerpt from a working /etc/sysconfig/iptables file. 
>> Redhatian users should recognize the first four lines.   This is where I
>> put it on my systems.  I still have to figure out how to make it hold
>> for longer than the 60 seconds.
> 
> I like that your solution fits within an existing firewall.
> 
> I'm too lazy to crank through somehting like that; I let BlockHosts put
> entries in the firewall and take them out after the 'cooling off
> period'.
> 
> http://aczoom.com/cms/blockhosts

Similar to the way denyhosts works.

I have used denyhosts.  Works fine as an after the fact block.  The down
side is the size of the hosts.deny gets to be.  This Iptables method
gets them on the fourth (or whatever) try.  I have had a situation where
a valid user got locked out.  I think it was the fault of the Windows
ssh/terminal software he was using.

I am thinking of trying a TARPIT instead of a DROP.  This will hold the
connection, won't let them disconnect, for 12-24 minutes according to
the man page.  So I'm thinking four tries in one minute and get held for
a bit.  :-)

Hopefully my fat fingers won't get me in trouble.


Rod

> 
> --Kurt

In-Reply-To: <20090120180517.8f4e1485.johnxj@comcast.net>
References: <3AC0BD2385F44FE2BCFC0E4B0E48B3DE@RAMA>	<20090117172550.GB10006@gate.kl-ic.com>	<868wp5mysw.fsf_-_@coulee.tdb.com>

Message-ID: <49793BCC.4030609@gmail.com>

John Jason Jordan wrote:

> Nevertheless, I crossed Seagate off my list.

All consumer drives suck. Every single brand. If you want far better
reliability, then get SAS drives and controllers. When you're dealing
with this stuff, support becomes a big issue. Seagate is dealing with
the issue and providing free data recovery service to boot. Their
warranties have been the best for a long time, and overall their
reliability sucks way less than the rest. I replace my personal IDE/SATA
drives after about three years.

From johnxj at comcast.net  Thu Jan 22 23:17:38 2009
From: johnxj at comcast.net (John Jason Jordan)
Date: Thu, 22 Jan 2009 23:17:38 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Feedback insanity
Message-ID: <20090122231738.cb24f350.johnxj@comcast.net>

You know how you sometimes get that feedback in a PA system? A whine
that changes as people move around or as the mike is positioned?

Well, after connecting my desktop to my stereo and setting it up so I
can use the computer as the sound source, I've got that now in my
study. It's driving me nuts.

Here's the weird part: There are no speakers anywhere near the corner
where the whine is emanating from. The speakers are on another wall and
pointed in another direction. What does exist in the location where the
sound comes from is the stereo receiver, a cable modem, an ethernet
switch and a router. And because of those devices there are quite a lot
of cables in the area.

I have completely disconnected the computer from the receiver by
pulling the cables out of the RCA input jacks. The sound continues. I
have turned the receiver completely off and the sound continues. Now,
with the receiver completely off there is no current going to the
speakers (at least nothing more than what the speaker wires might be
picking up from random rf in the room), so the sound cannot be coming
out of the speakers. And I mean it gets loud.

The only way to get relief is to lean back in my chair or otherwise
reposition myself. 

All I can conclude is that the modem, the switch or the router is
vibrating to produce the whine. The only other things in the corner of
the room where the sound comes from is wood, drywall and some paint.
Has anyone ever had such a device emit an audible feedback pitch? Any
other suggestions?

Unplug them each and wait perhaps 10 seconds to allow capacitors to 
drain?  When the sound stops, take that device in the next room (or 
otherwise plug it in by itself) and see if you can replicate it.

Are any of the wires wrapped around your stereo speaker wires?  But 
then, you said the sound isn't coming from the speakers. :-/

And failing all of that:  how loud is it?  Can you hear it over the 
stereo?  Is the stereo loud enough?

> whistle from the powered speakers on the PC, but listening closely it's 
> a radio station being picked up by the wiring. Keith I'm sure would have 
> a good explanation and solution to that problem.

The sound is not a radio station. It's exactly that variable wailing
whine you get when there is feedback in an old PA system. As I move my
body around the pitch and volume varies. And from past experience with
old PA systems, the position of the mic, speakers, and the mic gain are
related to the whine.

I thought Keith's suggestion to mute the mic on the desktop PC was
excellent. Unfortunately, having muted the mic in alsamixer, the whine
continues as before. For that matter, there is no microphone plugged in
on the PC. :(

It's really hard to troubleshoot because the slightest movement of my
body affects it. When it starts I want to get up and walk over to the
corner where it is coming from to feel the router, switch and modem
just to see if I can sense vibration from them. But the minute I move
the sound stops. Disconnecting any of them would kill my network. And I
might have to wait for a long time to see if the sound continues
because it is not always present.

The weird thing is that I sometimes get the sound even when the stereo
receiver is completely turned off. That means it has to be coming from
the router, modem or switch. It is also (barely) possible that it is
coming from the desktop PC, which is sitting on top of the table toward
that end of the room. For it to be coming from the PC the sound would
have to be echoing or somehow creating an auditory illusion that it is
coming from the corner. 

The PC is just a $50 box from Fry's with pretty standard stuff in it.
I'm not even sure the speaker in it is capable of making that much
sound. I don't even know where the speaker in it is located, except
that presumably it is toward the front of the case. That means it would
be facing away from the corner where I heard the sound coming from.

Troubleshooting something like this is maddening.

>
> The sound is not a radio station. It's exactly that variable wailing
> whine you get when there is feedback in an old PA system. As I move my
> body around the pitch and volume varies. And from past experience with
> old PA systems, the position of the mic, speakers, and the mic gain are
> related to the whine.
>
> I thought Keith's suggestion to mute the mic on the desktop PC was
> excellent. Unfortunately, having muted the mic in alsamixer, the whine
> continues as before. For that matter, there is no microphone plugged in
> on the PC. :(
>
> It's really hard to troubleshoot because the slightest movement of my
> body affects it. When it starts I want to get up and walk over to the
> corner where it is coming from to feel the router, switch and modem
> just to see if I can sense vibration from them. But the minute I move
> the sound stops. Disconnecting any of them would kill my network. And I
> might have to wait for a long time to see if the sound continues
> because it is not always present.
>
> The weird thing is that I sometimes get the sound even when the stereo
> receiver is completely turned off. That means it has to be coming from
> the router, modem or switch. It is also (barely) possible that it is
> coming from the desktop PC, which is sitting on top of the table toward
> that end of the room. For it to be coming from the PC the sound would
> have to be echoing or somehow creating an auditory illusion that it is
> coming from the corner.
>
> The PC is just a $50 box from Fry's with pretty standard stuff in it.
> I'm not even sure the speaker in it is capable of making that much
> sound. I don't even know where the speaker in it is located, except
> that presumably it is toward the front of the case. That means it would
> be facing away from the corner where I heard the sound coming from.
>
> Troubleshooting something like this is maddening.

Combined ground loop w/radio reception?
Is all the equipment plugged in using grounded plugs/receptacles?
Anything using 2 prong cords that don't have one side larger than the other?


From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Fri Jan 23 12:20:38 2009
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Fri, 23 Jan 2009 12:20:38 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Ahm Back -- Thanks To Help Here
Message-ID: <alpine.LNX.2.00.0901231206260.5231@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

   Finally got my main server/workstation booting and running
(Slackware-12.2) late this morning (and the notebook earlier this week). The
help and Slackware insight from Drew Wymore was absolutely invaluable, and
Dick Steffen's help as an intermediary to the list is also greatly
appreciated.

   Both Keith Lofstrom and Ed Borasky worked to indentify problems with the
notebook at last Sunday's clinic. A public "thank you" to them, too.

   The key issue with the notebook (after a few re-installations of -12.2)
turns out to be a missing module from the initial ram disk so it will boot
only from a monolithic kernel. This also turned out to be one issue on the
server/workstation, too. A fix for that will be implemented this weekend.

   The two key issues with the desktop were related to udev and the mtimes of
/etc files being newer than the mtimes of the same files on the new
installation of -12.2. In /etc/rc.d/rc.udev under -12.1 is the now-famous
string, "Triggering udev events: /sbin/udevtrigger". However, in -12.2,
there is no "/sbin/udevtrigger", but "/sbin/udevadm trigger". Critical
difference that I had to fix by hand since the USB flash drive was not
recognized as a device when I booted into the Slackware Disk #1.

   For the edification of other Slackware uses as inexperienced as SysAdmins
as I was, it's quite simple to use Disk #1 as a rescue/live disk. Boot as
though you want to install the distribution and when you log in as root,
make a new root-level directory (e.g., /slack), mount your hard drive's root
partition on that mount point (e.g., 'mount /dev/hda1 /slack'), then 'chroot
/slack'. Now you can mount other partitions on their normal mount points and
futz with the system unitl you figure out what needs to be repaired.

   Now to clean up the fuzzy edges and get back to work ....

Rich

   Is this some mis-configuration on my part, or is it a 'feature' of the
latest (and _very_ slow) release?

From creswick at gmail.com  Fri Jan 23 13:22:37 2009
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Fri, 23 Jan 2009 13:22:37 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Firefox-3.0.0.5 Issues
In-Reply-To: <alpine.LNX.2.00.0901231258140.5231@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <alpine.LNX.2.00.0901231258140.5231@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <c834ec80901231322s703cb19cmdfec6c7316197fda@mail.gmail.com>

On Fri, Jan 23, 2009 at 1:01 PM, Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> wrote:
>   Are others running firefox-3.x? That's replace the 2.x series in
> Slackware-12.2 and it is a major disappointment. When I open links from
> yesterday in the history sidebar the links are copied to the 'Today'
> section.

That happens here too, and seems to make sense.  (Granted, I never use
the history, so I could be misunderstanding something about the best
workflow..)

> But, as soon as I close the 'Yesterday' section, all of today's
> links are removed.

That does not seem to happen here, but maybe we're using different
"history" views.   There are too many links in each day's history to
make it worthwhile to have more than one day expanded at a time, but
even if I have today and yesterday expanded, collapsing either one has
no effect on the other.

>   Is this some mis-configuration on my part, or is it a 'feature' of the
> latest (and _very_ slow) release?

I've not noticed much difference in speed, but 3.x uses substantially
less ram than the 2.x series.  (meaning it only takes 600mb of ram,
rather than 1.2-1.6 gigs, and it's usage seems to be relatively
constant for my use patterns.)

I'd suggest getting a pre-compiled binary and try running it out of
your home directory to compare.  (Note that you will need to close
*all* existing instances of firefox before starting up the new version
or you will probably just spawn another window off of the old version
when you try to start the pre-compiled one.  There are ways to avoid
that, but it is much easier to just test them one at a time if you
don't *need* two instances running concurrently.)

Download:
http://www.mozilla.com/en-US/firefox/

--Rogan

From heinlein at madboa.com  Fri Jan 23 13:30:25 2009
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Fri, 23 Jan 2009 13:30:25 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Comcast Business Routers Exposed
Message-ID: <alpine.OSX.2.00.0901231320020.59035@guild.galois.com>

A colleague who should have known better had the NAT/firewall box 
that came with his Comcast Business account hacked today (and perhaps 
earlier).

I don't know the device make/model, but suffice it to say that it 
shipped with a default password (that he didn't change) and a web 
interface exposed to the wider Internet.

I had him shutdown and reset ASAP, so I don't know the complete 
extent of what the hacker (who resides in .cn) was able to accomplish, 
but at the very least they were able to muck with the built-in DHCP 
server, probably to facilitate DNS spoofing.

If you or your acquaintances have Comcast Business accounts, I suggest 
you verify that the router password (a) has been changed and (b) is 
what you expect. If not, shut down and ask Comcast how to get the box 
back to its factory settings -- and then change the password and, if 
possible, don't allow the world access to port 80.

Of course, the advice in the last paragraph applies to any router 
appliance, in Comcast-land or not.

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> http://www.madboa.com/

switches from D-Link.

> 
> Combined ground loop w/radio reception?
> Is all the equipment plugged in using grounded plugs/receptacles?
> Anything using 2 prong cords that don't have one side larger than the other?

Well, first off I can say that I am pretty sure it is not a ground loop
problem. If it was a ground loop wouldn't the frequency be 60 Hz? I
definitely know what a 60 Hz hum sounds like, and this is way higher -
around 2K Hz or so. 

As for two-prong plugs, everything in the area has three prong plugs
except the wall warts for the router, switch and modem. And they are
all polarized. And I wired the outlets myself when I redid the house
wiring a few years ago. The main panel has separate ground and common,
and the grounds are connected to two earth poles 20 feet apart, plus a
water bond. 

The wow-ee-wow sound it makes could be from rf. There are a lot of
electronic things in the room, so the possibility that stray rf is
being created is very high. Plus, the fact that the volume and pitch
changes as I move my body around sounds exactly like rf. But what on
earth could be receiving it and turning it into audio? I get the sound
even with the receiver turned off. That's the part that has me shaking
my head.

I did buy some new heavy duty speaker wire today. I've been planning on
replacing the wimpy stuff that's in the wall now anyway. When I
finished the remodeling I used 4x8 panels of 1/2 inch particle board
with screwed on bats instead of sheetrock so that I could open the wall
again. This wall has a lot of stuff in it - cable connection, for
example. I'm going to bore new holes for the speaker wires too. I doubt
that it'll make any difference though.

I'll keep poking at it. I can probably solve it just by repositioning
things over and over until it goes away. I'm just curious what is
causing it.

From aaron at madebyai.com  Fri Jan 23 17:51:30 2009

Subject: [PLUG] Postfix sender question
Message-ID: <200901231751.30601.aaron@madebyai.com>

Is there an easy way to have Postfix rewrite the From header on an outgoing 
message? Here's an example for clarification:

Cron is running a log check script which prints to standard out. Cron then 
takes the output and emails this to root, which is aliased to an external 
address. However, the From header looks like this:

From: root at somedomain.com (root)

This is confusing to people using certain email clients which expext the From 
line to look like this:

From: "Some Name" <root at somedomain.com>

Any assistance accomplishing this would be greatly appreciated!

-Aaron

Rich,

My understanding is that aliases are used for mail redirection, and have 
nothing to do with the From header that is attached to messages.

The problem is really with the mail clients in question, but I'm not able to 
change them out with more RFC compliant ones. It seems like cron is 
generating the mail header and piping the entire contents to a sendmail-esque 
wrapper provided by postfix. I don't really want to go mucking about in the 
source for that wrapper, there must be an option to have Postfix rewrite the 
From line itself.

Thanks,
Aaron

On Fri, Jan 23, 2009 at 4:59 PM, Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> wrote:
> On Fri, 23 Jan 2009, Rogan Creswick wrote:
>> I'd suggest getting a pre-compiled binary ...
>
>   That's what I'm using: the Slackware package.

Oof.  I probably *could* have been more cryptic, but it would have
taken substantial effort.

What I meant to recommend was running the mozilla-issued binary for
your platform, and comparing that.  Slackware *may* not have made any
alterations, but it's certainly possible that it was modified in some
subtle way that affected the performance.  (I've certainly noticed
differences between Iceweasle and Firefox, but that's not too
surprising.)

Anyway, the behavior you're seeing seems unusual to me, so that's the
first place I'd look.  It should also be pretty easy to test (you can

From heath at doublemarked.com  Fri Jan 23 22:09:48 2009
From: heath at doublemarked.com (Heath Morrison)
Date: Fri, 23 Jan 2009 22:09:48 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Postfix sender question
In-Reply-To: <200901231751.30601.aaron@madebyai.com>
References: <200901231751.30601.aaron@madebyai.com>
Message-ID: <746342180901232209o69f03f42x315788e79c7b81e4@mail.gmail.com>

Hey Aaron,

Postfix does provide a very simple way to do precisely what you're
describing. Check out the manpage for "header_checks".

Here's a quick rundown though:

1) Add this to /etc/postfix/main.cf:
   header_checks = pcre:/etc/postfix/header_checks.pcre
2) Add the following to /etc/postfix/header_checks.pcre:
  /^From: root at somedomain.com \(root\)/
    REPLACE From: "Some Name" <root at somedomain.com>
3) postfix reload

It works really well, and header_checks provides a variety of other
fun things that you can do to mail headers and bodies.

Now, regarding your actual problem. There may be a better approach
that deals more directly with the irritant - cron. Your cronjob
currently outputs to standard out and the cron manager is deciding how
to do the mail. Instead of that, manage the email yourself by  piping
your cronjob's output to /bin/mail. Try something like this:

* * * * * /usr/local/bin/my_cron_script | /bin/mail -s "Cronjob
Output" -r "Some Name <root at somedomain.com>" recipient at hostname.com

This should work well, and allows you to keep your cronjob mail hacks
inside the crontab instead of buried inside your MTA config.

Hope that helps!

-Heath

On Fri, Jan 23, 2009 at 5:51 PM, Aaron Ten Clay <aaron at madebyai.com> wrote:
> Is there an easy way to have Postfix rewrite the From header on an outgoing
> message? Here's an example for clarification:
>
> Cron is running a log check script which prints to standard out. Cron then
> takes the output and emails this to root, which is aliased to an external
> address. However, the From header looks like this:
>
> From: root at somedomain.com (root)
>
> This is confusing to people using certain email clients which expext the From
> line to look like this:
>
> From: "Some Name" <root at somedomain.com>
>
> Any assistance accomplishing this would be greatly appreciated!

> recognition modes or check for corrupted mail drop." A long time ago I set
> up poppler so she can retrieve mail over the local wireless connection. The
> current poppler package is installed. Where do I start looking for the
> clogged pipe on this issue?

the answer to both question is, in the system logs.  both poppler and
your MTA (not sure what slackware uses these days...probably postfix,
qmail, or sendmail i'd think, anyway, for this answer it doesn't
matter) should leave droppings in the logs.  if you have a separate
logfile for mail, they should even both be in there.

the "long sending delay" sounds like an MTA problem--sendmail
definitely used to do this if it had trouble with hostnames (when i've
experienced similar delay, it's been my own host that there's been
trouble doing DNS resolution of--localhost or the hostname sendmail is
configured to use for the system's hostname).

anyway, there's somewhere to start looking.  post logs if you got 'em
and they don't make things obvious (in the case of poppler i'd be
looking for failed login attempts or similar)

It would be interesting to slap a power meter on one.  The manual
says 30W max, and the animations on the D-Link website suggest
lower under idle and short cable conditions, but it does not say
how much lower. 

The theoretical minimum for a 16 port switch should be about 2W full
duplex all channels blazing, and close to zero watts for all channels
idle, so it would be nice to see where the D-Link is on the spectrum,
between the total of 18 Watts idle my pair of ancient Linksys 8 ports
(only 10/100) draw, and the theoretical minimum (which is almost
independent of link speed, BTW).

From jgw at tx0.org  Sat Jan 24 13:05:10 2009
From: jgw at tx0.org (Jeff_W)
Date: Sat, 24 Jan 2009 13:05:10 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Postfix sender question
In-Reply-To: <mailman.619.1232765026.25714.plug@lists.pdxlinux.org>
References: <mailman.619.1232765026.25714.plug@lists.pdxlinux.org>
Message-ID: <497b8286.jmNAfdrjHo2v6YwH%jgw@tx0.org>

Thiss works for me on NetBSD...

1) add the following to /etc/postfix/main.cf :
smtp_generic_maps = hash:/etc/postfix/generic

2) create/edit /etc/postfix/generic file:
root@<local_hostname>    uberadmin@<some_real_world_domain>

3) generate generic.db, do a check, then reload postfix configs:
# cd /etc/postfix
# sudo postmap generic
# sudo postfix check
# sudo /etc/rc.d/postfix reload


Perms on the various files:
-rw-r--r--  1 root  wheel     96 Sep 11 19:27 generic
-rw-r--r--  1 root  wheel  65536 Jan 14 23:56 generic.db
-r--r--r--  1 root  wheel    857 Jan 21 14:49 main.cf


Jeff

There are Ruby groups, PostgreSQL groups, Python groups, Drupal groups,
etc. here in town. They all have their own mailing lists, wikis, etc.
and meet in many of the same places we find ourselves gathering -- PSU,
CubeSpace, the Lucky Lab, Free Geek, OTBC ...

So my opinion is that we should keep the PLUG list focused on Linux, and
use more generic networking resources like Calagator and LinkedIn and
Twitter for non-Linux technologies.

Which version of VMware Player are you running? They upgraded not too
long ago. It might be worth heading to the VMware site and downloading a
fresh copy.

Also, "vmware-config.pl" does not exist in the most recent (6.5.1)
version of VMware *Workstation*. The new utility is called
"vmware-modconfig". Try (as root)

# vmware-modconfig --console --install-all

That should at least give you error messages. It should be in /usr/bin
if you need the whole path.

-- 
M. Edward (Ed) Borasky

I've never met a happy clam. In fact, most of them were pretty steamed.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Sat Jan 24 20:30:23 2009
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Sat, 24 Jan 2009 20:30:23 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Grandma Leeth's Restaurant
Message-ID: <20090125043023.GA24082@gate.kl-ic.com>

First off, I like the idea of Roots Organic Brewing company for
meetings; if that works out, we should have Advanced Topics 
(and perhaps afters) there.

However ...

My wife and I had dinner tonight in an unusual place - Grandma
Leeth's Restaurant ( www.grandmaleeths.com ) in the Cedar Hills
shopping center.   Saturday night is jazz night - I am hard of
hearing, and would rather hear my wife talk, so they seated us
upstairs.  A space about as big as Jax.  I asked, and the space
is available for meetings on weeknights.  

Leeth's is unusual because it is very family oriented.  The
downstairs space is half "play room" - actually, a place where
children between 2 and 9 can play and eat with childcare provided
by the restaurant.  Tonight they had three adult women down
there, supervising half a dozen kids,  while the kids' parents
ate with the grownups and listened to jazz.  Parents can sit
near the rail upstairs and glance down at their kids if they
wish.  Tonight, the parents didn't :-) .

As you would expect, this extra service raises the meal prices
a bit - adult entrees range from $11 to $18 or so.  They serve
beer and wine.  They call their food "world comfort food", and
I would call it "healthy upscale" - I had a paella, my wife
had lean angus beef on rice.  They provide for vegetarians
and gluten-free.  There are appetizers, so the impecunious
could get by on $7 or so.

They have free wifi (WEPed, sigh, but they provide the key).

Huge amounts of parking in the shopping center lot.  They are
about 800 feet from the Sunset Transit Center Max Station.
They are in Washington County, but the mailing address is
10122 SW Park Way, Portland so that still counts as "PLUG",
right?

So...

Most of the current PLUG attendance is guys without childcare
responsibilities.  I don't know how many potential members we
are missing because daddies and mommies can't come.  But if
we can recruit members from that group, I think that would be
worth an extra 30% meal cost.  This might also help us develop
some gender balance.

Please talk with your cow-orkers and friends, and other folks
that don't normally come to plug meetings, and see if this is
an attractive option.  We might try the place out with a
special "family Linux night" and see what kind of response we
get.  This could lead to a fourth meeting per month, focusing
on educational and family Linux topics.  Or, we might alternate
every other month between Advanced Topics at Roots and Family
Linux at Leeth's, providing some respite for Alan.

If this is worth pursuing, I will follow up.

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Sat Jan 24 22:25:30 2009

Subject: [PLUG] vmplayer virtual ethernet not working...

Message-ID: <20090125012530.zk96tjlf6skk8gkw-mazro@webmail.spamcop.net>

Quoting someone <plug_1 at robinson-west.com>:

> I am running VMware-Player-2.5.1-126130.i386.rpm
>
> and my kernel is:
>
> 2.6.27.9-73.fc9.i686 #1 SMP
>
> [root at silene modules]# /etc/init.d/vmware restart
> Stopping VMware services:
>     Virtual machine communication interface                 [  OK  ]
>     Virtual machine monitor                                 [  OK  ]
>     Blocking file system                                    [  OK  ]
> Starting VMware services:
>     Virtual machine monitor                                 [  OK  ]
>     Virtual machine communication interface                 [  OK  ]
>     Blocking file system                                    [  OK  ]
>     Virtual ethernet                                        [FAILED]
> [root at silene modules]#
>
> I have gone in as root and run
> vmware-modconfig --console --install-all
> manually.

Were there any error messages? It might not have built that module  
("vmnet", I think) correctly. Also, it probably did a "modprobe"  
trying to load the vmnet module. An "lsmod | more" should show it  
loaded. If it isn't there, look for errors in "dmesg" and try a  
"modprobe vmnet".

There's one other thing you might need to look at. After a fresh  
install, there may be a directory "/usr/lib/vmware/modules/binary". If  
there is, move it somewhere before doing the "vmware-modconfig" and  
see if that helps. That's a VMware bug of some kind -- it causes a  
more or less invisible segfault if that directory is present.

> I'm beginning to think that a patch is needed.

If it's the "invisible segfault", yes.

>What happens if you link the old to the new? ?Seems strange they would
>omit most of the packages.

What happens if you run `perl -e 'print "$_\n", for(@INC);'` ?

If you installed all of your modules with the help of the distribution, 
it should have upgraded them.  Otherwise, you should probably have the 
pure-perl modules in a directory without the 5.8.8 (and you could just 
keep using them), but you'll need to reinstall anything with binary 
extensions to get them to link on 5.10.

>> to load the vmnet module. An "lsmod | more" should show it loaded. If

Hmmm ... I just re-ran the vmware-modconfig:

Starting VMware services:
   Virtual machine monitor                                             done
   Virtual machine communication interface                             done
   Blocking file system                                                done
   Virtual ethernet                                                    done
   Shared Memory Available                                             done
Built vmmon module
Built vmnet module
Built vmblock module
Built vmci module
Built vsock module
DreamScape:~ # lsmod|grep vm
vmnet                  44868  13
vmblock                15744  3
vmci                   55560  0
vmmon                  76000  0
DreamScape:~ # lsmod|grep vs
DreamScape:~ #

So I don't have vsock loaded either, but mine is working. And of course

# /etc/init.d/vmware restart
Stopping VMware services:
   Virtual machine communication interface                          done
   Virtual machine monitor                                          done
   Blocking file system                                             done
Starting VMware services:
   Virtual machine monitor                                          done
   Virtual machine communication interface                          done
   Blocking file system                                             done
   Virtual ethernet                                                 done
   Shared Memory Available                                          done

So I looked at /etc/init.d/vmware and it says there is a log file in
/var/log/vnetlib. That gets appended rather than overwritten, so you
might want to do

cd /var/log
mv vnetlib vnetlib.bak
/etc/init.d/vmware restart

or whatever the equivalent is in Fedora. You should at least get an
error message that way.

In-Reply-To: <alpine.LNX.2.00.0901160846310.8095@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <alpine.LNX.2.00.0901160846310.8095@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Fri, 16 Jan 2009, Rich Shepard wrote:

>   Something broke yesterday afternoon and prevents me from syncing my PDA
> with jpilot on the desktop. Everything worked as usual through 2:53pm
> yesterday which was the last successful sync. Then it stopped working,
> with the jpilot.log showing:

   To close this thread on a happy note: it's all fixed now. After the
Troubles last week when I got the system back up with the new udev system
the PDA would still not sync with jpilot -- except for an exception
immediately after the first successful boot.

   Yesterday's experimentation determined that setting the port to usb:
(which did not work with earlier Slackware releases) now works like a charm.
Doesn't matter to which USB port the PDA is assigned, jpilot sees the
connection and they happily exchange vital bits.

# from Rich Shepard
# on Sunday 25 January 2009 18:14:

>[root at salmo ~]# /etc/rc.d/rc.spamassassin start
>/etc/rc.d/rc.spamassassin: /usr/bin/spamd: /usr/bin/perl5.8.8: bad
>interpreter: No such file or directory

Note that this particular error is a matter of the perl *binary* no 
longer existing.  I would typically expect an application to refer 
to /usr/bin/perl and you would maybe have a symlink from there to e.g. 
perl5.10.0.

In any case, the libraries (@INC, and libperl.so) and binary path are 
separate (but all important) issues involved in upgrading.

I'm somewhat surprised that your package manager didn't automatically 
resolve all of that when you upgraded the perl install.

--Eric

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Sun Jan 25 19:13:52 2009
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Sun, 25 Jan 2009 19:13:52 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Two machines versus one
Message-ID: <20090126031352.GA30318@gate.kl-ic.com>

The EEE PC Box is coming along - I reloaded it with Scientific
Linux 5.2 ( ~= RHEL5.2 or CentOS5.2 ) and the video is working
much better.  I have a Win2K VMware Player client running with
Dragon Naturally Speaking - I may recompile the host kernel
with some real time tweaks to see if we can get the accuracy up.

This machine will reside in my wife's office, where she will be
using it for dictations to create patient records.  My original
plan was to set up iptables to block all incoming traffic, only
outbound stuff allowed.  Since it is behind a NAT router, the
only threats are likely to be those carried in by firefox, and
zombied windoze machines on the same internal network.  We need
to make sure the patient records are 99.999% secure.  Right now
patient records are on paper, partly because of security risks
of digital records.  We would like to go digital if we can.

But my wife is not a security geek, and we are both concerned
that in the unlikely event of a successful exploit of a 
net-connected Linux machine, it may go unnoticed.  Not
acceptable.  Yes, you can run software that scans for exploits,
but it is better to have an airgap between the secure data 
and the net.  We can set up something where the data and the
net are not connected at the same time, but if the computer 
gets exploited while net connected, it can copy the data 
when it is not.  Very remote chance, but still there.

So we are considering setting up two machines, one connected
to the net, the other not, and select between them with a KVM
switch.  I'm testing that setup in her office right now.  With
this setup, she will be able to browse the web and do email 
and such with net-connected machine A, and use Dragon and do
secure stuff with isolated machine B, and switch between them
with a pushbutton.

There are problems with the printer sharing device I bought
(it turns out to be a stupid button actuated USB switch, and
HAL starts up a configuration dialog each time it is switched,
fooey!) and the two machine setup will need something more
printer-aware than that.  I am also bothered by the power waste
of two machines, and the inaccessability of machine B for
maintenance (right now, I maintain machine A through a VPN
from my home office).

I suppose another way to do this is to make TWO virtual machines
on host A, one that contains a linux guest running firefox, one
that contains the Win2K guest running Dragon (with net connections
turned off).  If the linux guest gets exploited via firefox, it
stays within the guest.  With the underlying host OS simplified
as much as possible, and set up to provide no services to the
local ethernet segment and potential zombies on it, that might
be suitably secure.  BTW, the Atom N270 used by the EEE PC Box
does not have virtualization instructions, so we can't use Xen.

So the question:  What am I missing here?  Are there good ways to
make one machine secure enough to do surfing and outbound vpn for
ssh, while keeping a VMware Windoze guest acceptably isolated?
Or, are there stupidities to avoid if I must use two machines?

Keith

BTW, physical security - the machines are physically connected
to the monitor, drives embedded behind a metal plate, and the
whole pile will be chained to the desk.  I suppose there could
be somebody a block away looking at this screen through a
telescope, but the windows are dirty!  There are paper records
in the hall, and a copy machine, and there are a few keys to the
office in circulation, so this is not defense-grade security. 
But I'm not looking for perfect security, just pretty good.

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From drew.wymore at gmail.com  Mon Jan 26 01:56:30 2009
From: drew.wymore at gmail.com (drew wymore)
Date: Mon, 26 Jan 2009 01:56:30 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] vsftpd + ldap folks around?
Message-ID: <e2aeccd60901260156q5e1c3371gc1fd21a9bb728c4d@mail.gmail.com>

I apologize in advance for the length of the message but I'm trying to
provide as much information as I possibly can.


I have been running openldap for about 5 years now and until now have never
had a problem. Specifically attempting to authenticate an FTP session is
failing in ways that I do not understand.

I am intermittently seeing this happen when attempting an ftp login ( yeah I
know ... from a Windows box -sigh- )

C:\Users\drew\Desktop>ftp
ftp> open techiekb.com
Connected to techiekb.com.
220 (vsFTPd 2.0.5)
User (techiekb.com:(none)): drew
331 Please specify the password.
Password:
500 OOPS: cannot locate user entry:drew
500 OOPS: child died
Connection closed by remote host.
ftp>

What I have been able to track down so far is that vsftpd is now looking for
users in /etc/passwd instead of using LDAP auth. I have LDAP configured via
nsswitch.conf which has worked wonderfully for years. All other services
that use LDAP (SSH, Apache, Squid) are all working fine.

When I don't receive that particular error message, I am able to login
(which tells me that vsftpd is talking to ldap somehow) but it's not pulling
proper group permissions so I can't upload anything to the server nor can
any of the people who are hosted on this machine.

There haven't been any recent package changes. And the configuration files
for vsftpd, inetd (which is what vsftpd was being run from until I decided
to run it in stand alone mode) are the same and nothing has changed in them
in _forever_, the LDAP configs have been changed recently to allow for TLS
support but the FTP service was working after those changes were made and
after LDAP was restarted with the new config, at the time of those changes
FTP was running out of inetd which had also been restarted and was working
fine.

The logs show that up until at least last Tuesday that authentication was
working as expected.

I did do the upgrade of vsftpd/inetd packages for my distro (Slackware) just
for grins and saw the same behaviour and went back to the original stock
packages that shipped with the version I'm running.

I enabled logging for vsftpd transactions and what is weird to me, is that
it shows the request, the response and OK event when the child spawned to
handle my request commits suicide, they seem to indicate that the client is
terminating the connection and not the host which is not the case. When it
*does* authenticate me and I attempt an upload, the logs show an OK status
as well even though the client reports that there was permission denied due
to the fact that the group/user perms aren't being pulled from the LDAP
server.

I'm stumped. I even ran strace on the binary while performing client to
server interaction and didn't see anything that looked out of place for the
behaviour I was seeing.

I have googled for the issue and there are various posts/solutions for it,
none of which have worked in my case. All the documentation I have found so
far indicates that PAM is required for this to work which I know to not be
the case since up until sometime last week apparently it was working fine. I
don't have PAM installed and won't install it unless I absolutely *have* to.
It's ommited from Slackware because of the numerous security flaws its been
a part of in the past, I'm not trying to start a my distro is better then
your distro conversation here though. The less complicated the better and
PAM just complicates things IMHO.

I have even restarted the box on the off chance something else was
interferring and that didn't help the cause either, other then losing 295
days of uptime =*(

Any thoughts, ideas, advice, voodoo chants?

Cheers,
Drew-

P.S.
Rich, we really need to go have that beer or 10.

applicable to you Ubuntu residents.

on the speakers.

From johnxj at comcast.net  Mon Jan 26 09:09:15 2009
From: johnxj at comcast.net (John Jason Jordan)
Date: Mon, 26 Jan 2009 09:09:15 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Ubuntu sound
In-Reply-To: <20090126141332.GA10756@jamhome.us>
References: <c834ec80901052317u24f82f92w4af19a6c40f85ea@mail.gmail.com>
	<20090126141332.GA10756@jamhome.us>
Message-ID: <20090126090915.8f652d2a.johnxj@comcast.net>

On Mon, 26 Jan 2009 06:13:32 -0800
Michael Rasmussen <michael at jamhome.us> dijo:

> This morning I follow the steps on:
> http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=789578&highlight=pulseaudio+fixes
> 
> And ... so far, so good.
> the page asserts that PulseAudio is the ESoundD replacement and the default
> confiration less something to be desired.

The page is essentially right, but the problems are manyfold. 

I have never had problems with sound disappearing on any of my
computers. It has always just worked - even with distros other than my
favorite Ubuntu x86_64. However, after upgrading my laptop from Hardy
to Intrepid I can no longer get sound to my bluetooth headphones. My
other bluetooth devices work fine (phone and mouse), but I haven't been
able to get so much as a beep out of the headphones for over a month.
They are paired up and connect fine but, regardless of the dozens of
fixes I have tried, the sound insists on coming out the speakers.

At the moment pulseaudio has been utterly excised from the computer.
Still no joy, though. All I can get is sound out the speakers. My
current route of inquiry is the confusing maze of stuff that goes on in
bluetooth.

Regarding pulseaudio, there are some optional packages that Ubuntu does
not install. Note, however, that Ubuntu started using pulseaudio with
Hardy and the configuration was the same. Some people have reported
success just by removing it - which is also complicated and I'll
explain how if you decide you want to try it. Pulseaudio does have some
terrific advantages over just ALSA and/or OSS. For example, you can set
sound levels differently for different apps, you can stream sound over
your network, and you can have more than one source playing at the same
time to more than one output device. I could, for example, play Obama's
inauguration speech from one app while having the Stars and Stripes
playing softly from another app, and capture the output with a third
app or device. 

Also remember that pulseaudio is a layer on top of ALSA. As far as I
can understand from the pages and pages of how-tos that I have read you
still need ALSA installed. Thus, you still have to contend with
alsamixer's confusing strangely named sliders and stuff.


From heinlein at madboa.com  Mon Jan 26 09:32:20 2009
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Mon, 26 Jan 2009 09:32:20 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Two machines versus one
In-Reply-To: <20090126031352.GA30318@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20090126031352.GA30318@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <alpine.OSX.2.00.0901260903410.69156@guild.galois.com>

On Sun, 25 Jan 2009, Keith Lofstrom wrote:

> This machine will reside in my wife's office, where she will be 
> using it for dictations to create patient records.  My original plan 
> was to set up iptables to block all incoming traffic, only outbound 
> stuff allowed.  Since it is behind a NAT router, the only threats 
> are likely to be those carried in by firefox, and zombied windoze 
> machines on the same internal network.  We need to make sure the 
> patient records are 99.999% secure.  Right now patient records are 
> on paper, partly because of security risks of digital records.  We 
> would like to go digital if we can.
>
> But my wife is not a security geek, and we are both concerned that 
> in the unlikely event of a successful exploit of a net-connected 
> Linux machine, it may go unnoticed.  Not acceptable.  Yes, you can 
> run software that scans for exploits, but it is better to have an 
> airgap between the secure data and the net.  We can set up something 
> where the data and the net are not connected at the same time, but 
> if the computer gets exploited while net connected, it can copy the 
> data when it is not.  Very remote chance, but still there.
>
> So we are considering setting up two machines, one connected to the 
> net, the other not, and select between them with a KVM switch.  I'm 
> testing that setup in her office right now.  With this setup, she 
> will be able to browse the web and do email and such with 
> net-connected machine A, and use Dragon and do secure stuff with 
> isolated machine B, and switch between them with a pushbutton.

Managing cross-domain connections -- in this case, HIPAA and non-HIPAA 
-- is hard. From personal experience I can tell you that the US 
government has put a LOT of money into researching and developing 
cross-domain solutions, but you'll still see

  * naval ships with several completely separate physical networks,
    even though space is at a premium,

  * intelligence employees with two or more computers on their
    desks, each machine connected to a different network (secure,
    secret, top secret, etc),

  * intelligence workers hand-typing data that has to move from
    one domain to another, since machines on one network cannot
    be allowed to operate on another.

Given the current state of technology, two machines is 
probably the safest bet. It's not the most efficient solution, but 
keeping patient data on machines accessible to a public network 
requires huge shovelfuls of vigilance, time your wife probably doesn't 
have to spare.

> I suppose another way to do this is to make TWO virtual machines on 
> host A, one that contains a linux guest running firefox, one that 
> contains the Win2K guest running Dragon (with net connections turned 
> off).  If the linux guest gets exploited via firefox, it stays 
> within the guest.  With the underlying host OS simplified as much as 
> possible, and set up to provide no services to the local ethernet 
> segment and potential zombies on it, that might be suitably secure. 
> BTW, the Atom N270 used by the EEE PC Box does not have 
> virtualization instructions, so we can't use Xen.

This is a reasonable solution -- but only if performance isn't a key 
concern and you both are comfortable with VM operations. A relatively 
underpowered Atom processor isn't going to make speed demons out of 
your virtual machines, and it can take some time to learning the in's 
and out's of VM administration.

> So the question:  What am I missing here?  Are there good ways to
> make one machine secure enough to do surfing and outbound vpn for
> ssh, while keeping a VMware Windoze guest acceptably isolated?
> Or, are there stupidities to avoid if I must use two machines?

It's a hard problem. The two-machine solution requires more space, 
more power, and has more breakable parts -- but it probably requires 
the least amount of admin time. A solution running VMs is elegant and 
efficient, except when it comes to administration (and perhaps 
processor utilization).

My bias is to use two machines until you and your wife are completely 
comfortable operating, maintaining, and troubleshooting VM issues -- 
though I'm willing to admit the issue is debatable and others may 
reasonably come to the opposite conclusion.

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> http://www.madboa.com/

that Comcast is doing deep packet inspection, recognizing the tracker
payload, and somehow replacing that with an empty response.

Message-ID: <20090126223917.5jczgaeoaos084o8-mazro@webmail.spamcop.net>

Quoting Michael Robinson <plug_1 at robinson-west.com>:

> I switched to vmware server 2.  It's a bit awkward though, I have to
> access it through a local web server and it took me a while to figure
> out how to get a screen from the virtual machine.  It's a lot more
> involved that player, there are more questions to answer.  I wonder
> if I can access the virtual machine from another computer on my
> network when I'm using vmware server?

If the virtual machine is set up as "bridged" and all your virtual and  
real network interfaces are working, yes. Just do an "ifconfig" in the  
guest, see what the IP address is, and it should just work.

VMware Server is a lot more flexible than the Player. You can actually  
create virtual machines with the server, while Player makes you create  
them elsewhere. But personally I think Workstation is worth paying for.

From merlyn at stonehenge.com  Tue Jan 27 22:44:17 2009
From: merlyn at stonehenge.com (Randal L. Schwartz)
Date: Tue, 27 Jan 2009 22:44:17 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] VOIP and Comcast
References: <497C21AD.7070204@gmail.com> <864ozlg993.fsf@blue.stonehenge.com>
Message-ID: <867i4gaq0u.fsf@blue.stonehenge.com>

>>>>> "Randal" == Randal L Schwartz <merlyn at stonehenge.com> writes:

Randal> Just a heads up for local folks... starting a few days ago, I appear
Randal> to be blocked on Comcast for all torrent traffic.  Just tested it with
Randal> the latest ubuntu distro seeded from ubuntu.org, so it's not about
Randal> "blocking illegal content".  I'm on the west side, and I'd be curious
Randal> to see if it's just me, or if others are also noticing this.

Randal> The symptom is that Transmission (on mac) reports "status 0" when it
Randal> tries to contact the tracker.  Normally, this is "status 200", so I
Randal> imagine that Comcast is doing deep packet inspection, recognizing the
Randal> tracker payload, and somehow replacing that with an empty response.

I tracked it down.  Turns out that up until the recent comcast update,
ipv6 travelled safely through my router to the nets.  Apparently, that's
now blocked, and the tracker had an ipv6 address being advertised, which
breaks if ipv6 isn't actually working.  My solution was to turn
off ipv6 on my laptop... when I get more time, I'll also turn it off
in my router so I'm not advertising v6 connections internally.

>>>>> "chris" == chris (fool) mccraw <gently at gmail.com> writes:

>> What are the ports called if you are using a USB to Serial adapter?

chris> if you use the usbserial driver, they should show up as ttyUSB0
chris> and ttyUSB1

Typically, although depending on the converter chip used, they might
show up elsewhere (e.g. /dev/ttyACM0).  Look in dmesg to see where it
landed with more certainty.

Windows XP Home edition or Pro?  If the former, then you need to enable 
guest access or enable per share passwords on the shares you want to 
access from this box. Windows "home edition" cannot be part of a domain 
(read crippled) for authentication purposes since it has no concept of 
user logins.

The 'invalid user nobody' message kinda points that way.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Thu Jan 29 18:28:27 2009
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Thu, 29 Jan 2009 18:28:27 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] turning off avahi
Message-ID: <20090130022827.GA15124@gate.kl-ic.com>

The distro I use, Scientific Linux 5.0, installs with the avahi
daemon enabled.  Avahi is the open source implementation of
Zeroconf aka Bonjour aka "link local".  Avahi chooses IP
addresses for machines on a network without a DHCP server,
discovers hardware like ethernet-connected printers, etc. 
In the abstract, a fine thing.

In reality, it sucks.  When I operate my laptop unconnected from
the wired network for a few minutes, avahi helpfully assigns an
ethernet address of 169.254.x.x to the port.  Which remains, even
after I plug an ethernet cable back in.  Of course, that address
is not routable on my network, nor can other machines find the
normally fixed DHCP-assigned IP address for my laptop.  That
means I have to stop and restart eth0.  That is broken, IMHO. 

So, I turned off the avahi daemon, and took it out of the boot
sequence.  Sadly,  I am told that the dark gods of dependency
hell have decreed that for the upcoming version 5.3 of my distro,
the cups print management software depends on cups-libs, which
depends on avahi-compat-libdns_sd, which depends on avahi, which
is enabled when it is installed.  Somebody needs a spanking.

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From drew.wymore at gmail.com  Thu Jan 29 21:54:15 2009
From: drew.wymore at gmail.com (drew wymore)
Date: Thu, 29 Jan 2009 21:54:15 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] vsftpd + ldap folks around? [RESOLVED]
Message-ID: <e2aeccd60901292154j3d498170x7bc730a6ce622872@mail.gmail.com>

On Mon, Jan 26, 2009 at 1:56 AM, drew wymore <drew.wymore at gmail.com> wrote:

> I apologize in advance for the length of the message but I'm trying to
> provide as much information as I possibly can.
>
>
> I have been running openldap for about 5 years now and until now have never
> had a problem. Specifically attempting to authenticate an FTP session is
> failing in ways that I do not understand.
>
> I am intermittently seeing this happen when attempting an ftp login ( yeah
> I know ... from a Windows box -sigh- )
>
> C:\Users\drew\Desktop>ftp
> ftp> open techiekb.com
> Connected to techiekb.com.
> 220 (vsFTPd 2.0.5)
> User (techiekb.com:(none)): drew
> 331 Please specify the password.
> Password:
> 500 OOPS: cannot locate user entry:drew
> 500 OOPS: child died
> Connection closed by remote host.
> ftp>
>
> What I have been able to track down so far is that vsftpd is now looking
> for users in /etc/passwd instead of using LDAP auth. I have LDAP configured
> via nsswitch.conf which has worked wonderfully for years. All other services
> that use LDAP (SSH, Apache, Squid) are all working fine.
>
<snip>

Let me first apologize for the post to the list. But I think it's fair
enough to put the info here so it will be archived in case someone else runs
across this issue in the future.

 5 days, many virtual machine re-installs for environment testing, log
reading on the actual machine affected, packing installs, package removals,
restarting daemons, restarting the affected machine, rebuilding packages
from source with different build options, banging my head on the wall,
angrily shaking my fist and cursing ... and I finally found the culprit.

It turned out to be slapd the Open LDAP daemon. What threw me off track was
the fact that no other services appeared to be affected, just vsftpd so I
focused on it. Unfortunately it doesn't provide much useful log information
when logins fail so finding the issue was by sure luck. I ended up greping
the entire /var/log directory for "vsftpd" and found one entry of interest
from January 25th. I believe it was in a log that was overwritten after I
updated a few things tonight to solve the issue but it in effect said
"vsftpd unable to contact LDAP server, decode error".

So googling for LDAP and decode error pointed me to a few posts that said
nss_ldap was the issue, nss_ldap allows for system and service wide
authentication to LDAP databases. So I upgraded to the latest version and
found it still wasn't working, it then occurred to me that maybe it was Open
LDAP itself. Investingating that led me to find that another person who I
allow to administer the machine had done some house cleaning and removed the
version of Berkley DB that Open LDAP was linked against ... AHA!

So I rebuilt Open LDAP against the installed libraries and then nss_ldap
against the newly minted and properly linked LDAP libs and all was well.

All the vsftpd searches for the error I was receiving pointed to issues with
PAM and that PAM was needed for vsftpd to auth against a directory server,
this isn't true. The NSS_LDAP libraries from www.padl.com negate the need to
build PAM support for it which is why it has worked well for so long and
added to my frustration in troubleshooting the issue.

Cheers,
Drew-

p.s. Now I just need to help ressucitate Rich Shepard's machine and life
will be all good once again in Linux Land.

I've been colocated there for more than 5 years.  It used to be okay but
nowadays the service has gone bad in my opinion.  For example, I had two
full cabinets which I no longer use.  When the renewal date approached, I
gave about 40 day advance written notice that I didn't want to renew.  Now
they're trying to make me pay more than $10,000 for the next few years of
service, stating I didn't give them enough notice that I wasn't renewing my
contract.  That's just greed in my opinion.

A long time before that I had a certain amount of bandwidth agreed upon per
cabinet, they later said that no, that was a mistake on their part, and
proceeded to cut my alloted bandwidth by 75% thereby making me pay about
$1000/month extra for bandwidth that I already had in my opinion, and in
writing from them earlier.

The most recent action is an almost 100% price increase for the private cage
i had there.  Their contracts state they can raise their prices by any
amount at anytime and you have no recourse whatsoever.  The only way out is
to pay the entire remainder even if you have years left on your contract.

I had to get a lawyer to deal with them and it's still ongoing.  I know two
other people who were also colocated with Infinity Internet and had similar
experiences, one of whom also had to get a lawyer involved.

IMO, grab your servers and run away as fast as you can.   Try the Pittock
Internet Exchange across the street.

Jon Daniels
Owner, Fork Networking

From ramunro at speakeasy.net  Fri Jan 30 23:14:36 2009
From: ramunro at speakeasy.net (Robert Munro)
Date: Fri, 30 Jan 2009 23:14:36 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] turning off avahi
In-Reply-To: <mailman.876.1233340910.25714.plug@lists.pdxlinux.org>
References: <mailman.876.1233340910.25714.plug@lists.pdxlinux.org>
Message-ID: <1233386076.5616.19.camel@eris>

> Date: Thu, 29 Jan 2009 18:28:27 -0800
> From: Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com>
> Subject: [PLUG] turning off avahi
> To: PLUG <plug at lists.pdxlinux.org>
> Message-ID: <20090130022827.GA15124 at gate.kl-ic.com>
> Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii
> 
> The distro I use, Scientific Linux 5.0, installs with the avahi
> daemon enabled.  Avahi is the open source implementation of
> Zeroconf aka Bonjour aka "link local".  Avahi chooses IP
> addresses for machines on a network without a DHCP server,
> discovers hardware like ethernet-connected printers, etc. 
> In the abstract, a fine thing.
> 
> In reality, it sucks.  When I operate my laptop unconnected from
> the wired network for a few minutes, avahi helpfully assigns an
> ethernet address of 169.254.x.x to the port.  Which remains, even
> after I plug an ethernet cable back in.  Of course, that address
> is not routable on my network, nor can other machines find the
> normally fixed DHCP-assigned IP address for my laptop.  That
> means I have to stop and restart eth0.  That is broken, IMHO. 
> 
> So, I turned off the avahi daemon, and took it out of the boot
> sequence.  Sadly,  I am told that the dark gods of dependency
> hell have decreed that for the upcoming version 5.3 of my distro,
> the cups print management software depends on cups-libs, which
> depends on avahi-compat-libdns_sd, which depends on avahi, which
> is enabled when it is installed.  Somebody needs a spanking.
> 
> Keith

Mandriva, which I run, installs avahi by default as well.  Since I too
don't need zeroconf network discovery, I've simply taken avahi-daemon
out of the init-scripts (actually I turned it off with the system GUI).

That seems to work, though I'd rather remove the avahi package entirely.

Adding NOZEROCONF=yes to /etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/ifcfg-eth0 also
works to prevent the system from setting 169.254.x.x network addresses.

I agree that distros tacking on zeroconf, wireless and other networking
related packages is a pain - especially when dependencies get involved.

Robert
